class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-body2 ent-css-10xi6sq"><span>Published <!-- -->August 24, 2020. </span></p></div><div class="ent-tss-8gyp5s-postedTimeCommentsWrapper"></div><div class="ent-tss-71r2e1-mainImageWrapper"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img loading="eager" id="ent-blog-image" class="ent-tss-32jtuo-previewCover-image" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/700x700/Untitled_Presentation_8-1741610713539.jpg" alt="a screenshot of a computer screen with a green message" width="680" height="383"><button class="MuiButtonBase-root MuiIconButton-root MuiIconButton-sizeMedium ent-tss-yjupvi-expandIcon ent-tss-45-expandIcon-ref ent-css-1yxmbwk" tabindex="0" type="button"><svg class="MuiSvgIcon-root MuiSvgIcon-fontSizeMedium ent-css-vubbuv" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewbox="0 0 24 24" data-testid="OpenInFullIcon"><path d="M21 11V3h-8l3.29 3.29-10 10L3 13v8h8l-3.29-3.29 10-10z"></path></svg></button></div></div></div><div class="ent-tss-g7g134-blogContentWrapper"><div class="ent-tss-o5kd66-enContentEditor en-content"><div id="ent-blog-content" class="ent-tss-16bdfpw-editable" data-slate-editor="true" data-slate-node="value" contenteditable="false" zindex="-1" style="position:relative;outline:none;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word"><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">On August 9, 2020, Torum’s administrator announced the forum is shutting down. What was this forum, and will its users find alternatives? KELA explored various darknet sources, as well as Torum itself, to find out. Here is a summary of our findings:</span></span></span></p><ul data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-1jjvw86-listDisc"><li data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Torum was an English-speaking underground forum that posed as a nonprofit cybersecurity website. While both its members and users of other forums agreed Torum </span></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">was a good place to discuss cybersecurity and learn hacking methods, the site was overwhelmed by newbies and scammers who damaged its reputation.</span></strong></span></span></li><li data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">Torum’s administrator announced he is closing the forum because he lost interest in supporting it.</span></strong></span></span></li><li data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">Torum was an active, stable community, which will likely be missed by users. </span></strong></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The forum has </span></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">a few alternatives in the darknet, including CryptBB, which recently became public</span></strong></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">. This post will explore what distinguished Torum and what darknet chatter reveals about possible alternatives.</span></span></span></li><li data-slate-node="element"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">As users struggle to find new forums with a decent community, </span></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">it is crucial to continue tracking these sources to understand new trends and TTPs, and proactively mitigate potential risks emerging from them.</span></strong></span></span></li></ul><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" Torum shutting down" title="The announcement of Torum shutting down" width="680" height="368"></noscript><button class="MuiButtonBase-root MuiIconButton-root MuiIconButton-sizeMedium data-slate-length="0">﻿</span></span></span></div></div><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:center"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><em><span data-slate-string="true">The announcement of Torum shutting down</span></em></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="the-history-of-torum"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The History of Torum</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Launched in May 2017, Torum reportedly had more than 130,000 users, a substantial number for an underground forum. RaidForums, the most popular English-speaking forum, has about 465,000 members, 15,000 active daily.</span></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Torum only gained popularity among the English-speaking audience in February 2019, when Kickass (an English-speaking platform for cybercriminals) went offline. Torum’s user base </span></span></span><a data-slate-node="element" href="https://www.digitalshadows.com/blog-and-research/forums-are-forever-part-1-cybercrime-never-dies/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" class="ent-tss-p16xa7-link"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">increased</span></span></span></a><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true"> by 639% from February to October of that year.</span></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">We used KELA’s DARKBEAST to dive into Torum’s posts, concluding it was actively maintained throughout 2020, with almost 95,000 posts published from January to August. Based on our analysis, in addition to cybersecurity discussions, many conversations focused on malicious activities and other related information, as well as trading and sharing accesses and databases.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20680%20420'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Torum’s activity in 2020 (number of messages)" title="Torum’s activity in 2020 (number of messages)" width="680" height="420" data-lazy-src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x420/23-1739355196027.png"><noscript><img style="width:100% !important" loading="lazy" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x420/23-1739355196027.png" alt="Torum’s activity in 2020 (number of messages)" data-slate-length="0">﻿</span></span></span></div></div><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:center"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><em><span data-slate-string="true">Torum’s activity in 2020 (number of messages)</span></em></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The official reason for closure, provided by Torum’s administrator, is that he “lost the passion” to maintain the forum. We found nothing indicating otherwise. Torum was known for frequent outages: members mentioned the site could be down for a few days at a time, suggesting the administrator wasn’t rushing to fix technical issues. Some users also said the administrator was tired of the flood of spam messages on Torum.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20680%20437'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="A message posted on Onion Links, a Telegram channel dedicated to darknet news: “In particular, the closure of the site is associated with constant spam, which was barely sorted out by the moderators. Others still paid respect to the forum: “Torum had it all – wacky stuff, DNM related content, discussion on fraud, scripting, hacking, cracking, and of course shitposts. For many, it was the community that introduced them to the concepts of NetSec and fraud.”</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% data-slate-leaf="true"><em><span data-slate-string="true">A user discussing the closure of Torum on (source: Dread, “the darknet Reddit”)</span></em></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">It appears that Torum had loyal members, who rarely posted on other underground forums, at least with the same user handles.</span></strong></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true"> Torum’s ten most active users used 2-3 other forums on average, with Torum as their primary platform.</span></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">So what types of data were sold on Torum, and what interested its members?</span></strong></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true"> Here’s a quick review of the topics discussed in July 2020:</span></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="hacking-and-cybersecurity"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Hacking and Cybersecurity</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Users often asked for advice from experienced users, and the forum was considered a place where one could learn hacking. Here are a few recent examples of such questions: “What can I do with IP address?”, “Have CC [credit card data] + info – now what?”, “Is it possible to get into someone’s iPhone camera and spy on them?” Torum claimed to be a place for in-depth discussions about cybersecurity, but these conversations were much less common. However, some users referred to Torum members as experienced hackers. Besides hacking, community members discussed general interest topics, such as Covid-19.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:center"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><em><span data-slate-string="true">Discussions about darknet websites (source: Dread)</span></em></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="databases-for-sale-and-free"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Databases for Sale and Free</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Torum users shared popular recent leaks (Tokopedia breach and BlueLeaks, for example), as well as exclusive findings. For instance, one user posted data stolen from an Irish financial company, and others pointed out the company’s site has an XSS vulnerability. Users shared databases in the forum’s Intel exchange section, open for members who posted ten messages on Torum.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" 11V3h-8l3.29 3.29-10 10L3 13v8h8l-3.29-3.29 10-10z"></path></svg></button></div></div> <div data-slate-spacer="true" style="height:0;color:transparent;outline:none;position:absolute"><span DARKBEAST)</span></em></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="accounts-remote-access-and-credit-card-data-for-sale"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Accounts, Remote Access and Credit Card Data for Sale</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Various users were looking to buy and sell remote access to organizations, accounts of financial services (including WebMoney, Exmo, PayPal, Yandex Money), and other types of data. Based on their offering, we assume sellers didn’t use Torum as an exclusive trading platform.</span></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="malware-for-sale"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Malware for Sale</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Thanos ransomware, which emerged in late 2019, attracted the attention of Torum users debating whether the author of a post advertising it should be trusted. He identified as the developer of Thanos, who decided to offer it to Torum’s users. Exploits, RATs, ATM malware, and other malicious tools were also discussed and offered for sale.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20680%20245'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="The developer of Thanos ransomware offered his product on Torum (via DARKBEAST)" title="The developer of Thanos ransomware offered his product on Torum (via DARKBEAST)" width="680" height="245" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x245/81-1739355575089.png" alt="The developer of Thanos ransomware offered his product on Torum (via DARKBEAST)" title="The developer of Thanos ransomware offered his product on Torum (via DARKBEAST)" width="680" height="245"></noscript><button class="MuiButtonBase-root MuiIconButton-root MuiIconButton-sizeMedium ent-tss-yjupvi-expandIcon ent-tss-45-expandIcon-ref ent-css-1yxmbwk" tabindex="0" type="button"><svg class="MuiSvgIcon-root MuiSvgIcon-fontSizeMedium ent-css-vubbuv" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewbox="0 0 24 24" data-testid="OpenInFullIcon"><path d="M21 11V3h-8l3.29 3.29-10 10L3 13v8h8l-3.29-3.29 10-10z"></path></svg></button></div></div> <div data-slate-spacer="true" style="height:0;color:transparent;outline:none;position:absolute"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-zero-width="z" data-slate-length="0">﻿</span></span></span></div></div><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:center"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><em><span data-slate-string="true">The developer of Thanos ransomware offered his product on Torum (via DARKBEAST)</span></em></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">As can be seen, the data offered on Torum were rarely unique. However, users valued it as a place for hacking-related conversations and learning. Torum had a private section for administrators and moderators of the forum, but it was closed following leaks of private discussions. Now, both veterans and newbies must find a new platform for similar discussions.</span></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="where-will-users-migrate"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Where Will Users Migrate?</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Most users have been probably already using other platforms and markets dedicated to leaks, malware, tools, etc. </span></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">Torum was never famous for being the first source for such offers, so users will look for a new place to discuss hacking activities. Here are the leading alternatives:</span></strong></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">According to darknet chatter, a prospective replacement is </span></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><strong><span data-slate-string="true">CryptBB</span></strong></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">, which recently </span></span></span><a data-slate-node="element" href="https://www.digitalshadows.com/blog-and-research/cryptbb-demystifying-the-illusion-of-the-private-forum/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" class="ent-tss-p16xa7-link"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">eased</span></span></span></a><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true"> the acceptance process of new users. CryptBB, launched in 2017, started as a private English-speaking hacking forum known for its rigorous application policy, only accepting members who pass an interview. However, in late 2019, CryptBB opened a section for “newbies” who are not skilled enough to be accepted but still want to learn from experienced hackers, posting a thread on Dread, where administrators invite beginners to improve their skills and evolve into “pro” members.</span></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">CryptBB has around 10,000 users, but when users struggle to find forums with a decent community, the application process and the semi-private mode might attract new users. Even on Torum, members were looking for platforms with a strict screening process, including Exodus, an exclusive forum that was closed in 2017.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20680%20189'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="A user interested in an alternative to Exodus (source: Torum; via DARKBEAST)" title="A user interested in an alternative to Exodus (source: Torum; via DARKBEAST)" width="680" height="189" data-lazy-src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x189/91-1739355629836.png"><noscript><img style="width:100% !important" loading="lazy" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x189/91-1739355629836.png" alt="A user interested in an alternative to Exodus (source: Torum; via DARKBEAST)</span></em></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">As CryptBB seems focused on gaining a larger audience and building a new brand on the darknet, Torum’s closure is a positive development. Some users are already recommending CryptBB as a replacement.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" source, revealing relationships between prominent hackers who share information about new TTPs.</span></strong></span></span><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span {"tags":[],"loaded":false,"popularTags":[]},"category":{"page":null,"pageLoaded":false},"topic":{"tag":null,"tagLoaded":false},"redirect":{"url":null,"name":null,"message":null,"redirectHttpCode":null},"page":{"post":{"previewImage":{"height":1080,"width":1920,"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fentail-assets.com\u002Fkelacyber\u002FUntitled_Presentation_8-1741610713539.jpg","alt":"a screenshot of a computer screen with a green message","title":"Torum is Dead. Long Live CryptBB?","caption":"a screenshot of a computer screen with a green message"},"previewVideo":null,"locale":"en","variant":"default","brief":null,"briefRichText":null,"showTOC":true,"showCoverImage":true,"title":"Torum is Dead. Long Live CryptBB?","richTitle":null,"subtitle":null,"richSubtitle":null,"text":"On August 9, 2020, Torum’s administrator announced the forum is shutting down. What was this forum, and will its users find alternatives? KELA explored various darknet sources, as well as Torum itself, to find out. Here is a summary of our findings:\nTorum was an English-speaking underground forum that posed as a nonprofit cybersecurity website. While both its members and users of other forums agreed Torum was a good place to discuss cybersecurity and learn hacking methods, the site was overwhelmed by newbies and scammers who damaged its reputation.Torum’s administrator announced he is closing the forum because he lost interest in supporting it.Torum was an active, stable community, which will likely be missed by users. The forum has a few alternatives in the darknet, including CryptBB, which recently became public. This post will explore what distinguished Torum and what darknet chatter reveals about possible alternatives.As users struggle to find new forums with a decent community, it is crucial to continue tracking these sources to understand new trends and TTPs, and proactively mitigate potential risks emerging from them.\n\nThe announcement of Torum shutting down\nThe History of Torum\nLaunched in May 2017, Torum reportedly had more than 130,000 users, a substantial number for an underground forum. RaidForums, the most popular English-speaking forum, has about 465,000 members, 15,000 active daily.\nTorum only gained popularity among the English-speaking audience in February 2019, when Kickass (an English-speaking platform for cybercriminals) went offline. Torum’s user base increased by 639% from February to October of that year.\nWe used KELA’s DARKBEAST to dive into Torum’s posts, concluding it was actively maintained throughout 2020, with almost 95,000 posts published from January to August. Based on our analysis, in addition to cybersecurity discussions, many conversations focused on malicious activities and other related information, as well as trading and sharing accesses and databases.\n\nTorum’s activity in 2020 (number of messages)\nThe official reason for closure, provided by Torum’s administrator, is that he “lost the passion” to maintain the forum. We found nothing indicating otherwise. Torum was known for frequent outages: members mentioned the site could be down for a few days at a time, suggesting the administrator wasn’t rushing to fix technical issues. Some users also said the administrator was tired of the flood of spam messages on Torum.\n\nWas Torum Unique?\nAccording to users’ complaints on other forums, Torum featured many beginners asking “noob questions” and scammers posting malicious links. When discussing Torum shutting down, some mentioned it wasn’t such a loss. Others still paid respect to the forum: “Torum had it all – wacky stuff, DNM related content, discussion on fraud, scripting, hacking, cracking, and of course shitposts. For many, it was the community that introduced them to the concepts of NetSec and fraud.”\n\nUsers discussing the closure of Torum (source: darknet forum TheHub)\n\nA user discussing the closure of Torum on (source: Dread, “the darknet Reddit”)\nIt appears that Torum had loyal members, who rarely posted on other underground forums, at least with the same user handles. Torum’s ten most active users used 2-3 other forums on average, with Torum as their primary platform.\nSo what types of data were sold on Torum, and what interested its members? Here’s a quick review of the topics discussed in July 2020:\nHacking and Cybersecurity\nUsers often asked for advice from experienced users, and the forum was considered a place where one could learn hacking. Here are a few recent examples of such questions: “What can I do with IP address?”, “Have CC [credit card data] + info – now what?”, “Is it possible to get into someone’s iPhone camera and spy on them?” Torum claimed to be a place for in-depth discussions about cybersecurity, but these conversations were much less common. However, some users referred to Torum members as experienced hackers. Besides hacking, community members discussed general interest topics, such as Covid-19.\n\nDiscussions about darknet websites (source: Dread)\nDatabases for Sale and Free\nTorum users shared popular recent leaks (Tokopedia breach and BlueLeaks, for example), as well as exclusive findings. For instance, one user posted data stolen from an Irish financial company, and others pointed out the company’s site has an XSS vulnerability. Users shared databases in the forum’s Intel exchange section, open for members who posted ten messages on Torum.\n\nDatabase leaks on Torum (via DARKBEAST)\nAccounts, Remote Access and Credit Card Data for Sale\nVarious users were looking to buy and sell remote access to organizations, accounts of financial services (including WebMoney, Exmo, PayPal, Yandex Money), and other types of data. Based on their offering, we assume sellers didn’t use Torum as an exclusive trading platform.\nMalware for Sale\nThanos ransomware, which emerged in late 2019, attracted the attention of Torum users debating whether the author of a post advertising it should be trusted. He identified as the developer of Thanos, who decided to offer it to Torum’s users. Exploits, RATs, ATM malware, and other malicious tools were also discussed and offered for sale.\n\nThe developer of Thanos ransomware offered his product on Torum (via DARKBEAST)\nAs can be seen, the data offered on Torum were rarely unique. However, users valued it as a place for hacking-related conversations and learning. Torum had a private section for administrators and moderators of the forum, but it was closed following leaks of private discussions. Now, both veterans and newbies must find a new platform for similar discussions.\nWhere Will Users Migrate?\nMost users have been probably already using other platforms and markets dedicated to leaks, malware, tools, etc. Torum was never famous for being the first source for such offers, so users will look for a new place to discuss hacking activities. Here are the leading alternatives:\nAccording to darknet chatter, a prospective replacement is CryptBB, which recently eased the acceptance process of new users. CryptBB, launched in 2017, started as a private English-speaking hacking forum known for its rigorous application policy, only accepting members who pass an interview. However, in late 2019, CryptBB opened a section for “newbies” who are not skilled enough to be accepted but still want to learn from experienced hackers, posting a thread on Dread, where administrators invite beginners to improve their skills and evolve into “pro” members.\nCryptBB has around 10,000 users, but when users struggle to find forums with a decent community, the application process and the semi-private mode might attract new users. Even on Torum, members were looking for platforms with a strict screening process, including Exodus, an exclusive forum that was closed in 2017.\n\nA user interested in an alternative to Exodus (source: Torum; via DARKBEAST)\nAs CryptBB seems focused on gaining a larger audience and building a new brand on the darknet, Torum’s closure is a positive development. Some users are already recommending CryptBB as a replacement.\n\nA thread on HiddenAnswers, the darknet alternative of Quora\nCryptBB’s contenders include TheHub, claiming to have around 157,000 users, who are supposedly less into hacking activities and not as active as Torum’s users. We traced about 16,000 messages posted in 2020 – while Torum had almost 95,000.\n\na screenshot of users discussing an alternative to Torum (source: TheHub)\n\nA now-deleted thread discussing Torum (source: TheHub; via DARKBEAST)\nEven before Torum shut down, some users mentioned alternative darknet forums: Dread, Nulled, Cracked, Helium, HackTown, HackForums, Envoy, and some Russian-speaking forums.\nWhile Torum and its alternatives are not where critical leaks are posted every day, they are a valuable source, revealing relationships between prominent hackers who share information about new TTPs. This data could be even more useful than the results of the hacking activities (e.g., leaks) as it can help prevent attacks.","richText":"[{\"type\":\"paragraph\",\"children\":[{\"text\":\"On August 9, 2020, Torum’s administrator announced the forum is shutting down. What was this forum, and will its users find alternatives? KELA explored various darknet sources, as well as Torum itself, to find out.             <script>

        // if getParameterByName function is not defined, define it
        if (typeof getParameterByName === 'undefined') {
            function getParameterByName(name, url) {
                if (!url) url = window.location.href;
                name = name.replace(/[\[\]]/g, "\\$&");
                var regex = new RegExp("[?&]" + name + "(=([^&#]*)|&|#|$)"),
                    results = regex.exec(url);
                if (!results) return null;
                if (!results[2]) return '';
                return decodeURIComponent(results[2].replace(/\+/g, " "));
            }
        }

        jQuery(document).ready(function($) {

            // First detect if _GET params are present.
            // We only need utm_source, utm_medium and utm_campaign
            var utm_source = getParameterByName('utm_source');
            var utm_medium = getParameterByName('utm_medium');
            var utm_campaign = getParameterByName('utm_campaign');
            var utm_content = getParameterByName('utm_content');
            var utm_term = getParameterByName('utm_term');

            // Next we will use Cookies.js to set cookies

            // If _GET params are present, set cookies
            if (utm_source) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_source', utm_source, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_medium) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_medium', utm_medium, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_campaign) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_campaign', utm_campaign, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_content) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_content', utm_content, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_term) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_term', utm_term, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }

            // Check if cookies are present
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_source')) {
                utm_source = Cookies.get('kela_utm_source');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_medium')) {
                utm_medium = Cookies.get('kela_utm_medium');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_campaign')) {
                utm_campaign = Cookies.get('kela_utm_campaign');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_content')) {
                utm_content = Cookies.get('kela_utm_content');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_term')) {
                utm_term = Cookies.get('kela_utm_term');
            }

            // Wait 4 seconds for the form to load
            setTimeout(function() {
                
                // Find if hidden fields exist, for example: .hs-utm_campaign input
                if ($(".hs-utm_source input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_source input").val(utm_source);
                }
                if ($(".hs-utm_medium input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_medium input").val(utm_medium);
                }   

                if ($(".hs-utm_campaign input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_campaign input").val(utm_campaign);
                }

                if ($(".hs-utm_content input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_content input").val(utm_content);
                }

                if ($(".hs-utm_term input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_term input").val(utm_term);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_source input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_source input").val(utm_source);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_medium input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_medium input").val(utm_medium);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_campaign input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_campaign input").val(utm_campaign);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_content input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_content input").val(utm_content);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_term input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_term input").val(utm_term);
                }
                
            }, 4000);

            
        });
